#PROJECT
PR:PROJECT_TITLE                 	Metabolomic Profiling in Early Pregnancy using Pre-Diagnostic Sera from Women
PR:PROJECT_TITLE                 	Who Developed Placental Abruption
PR:PROJECT_TYPE                  	Metabolomics
PR:PROJECT_SUMMARY               	Placental abruption is an ischemic placental disorder that results from the
PR:PROJECT_SUMMARY               	premature separation of the placenta from the wall of the uterus before delivery
PR:PROJECT_SUMMARY               	of the fetus. This disorder is associated with pre-term delivery, fetal death,
PR:PROJECT_SUMMARY               	maternal hemorrhagic shock, and renal failure. Several physiologic disturbances,
PR:PROJECT_SUMMARY               	such as oxidative stress, carbohydrate/fatty acid metabolism, and mitochondrial
PR:PROJECT_SUMMARY               	dysfunction, have been associated with ischemic placental disorder as well as
PR:PROJECT_SUMMARY               	with placental abruption. This preliminary study proposes to identify
PR:PROJECT_SUMMARY               	metabolites associated with incident placental abruption using existing serum
PR:PROJECT_SUMMARY               	and clinical data from a previously studied cohort. Metabolomics analysis will
PR:PROJECT_SUMMARY               	be carried out on maternal serum (51 cases and 51 controls) collected in early
PR:PROJECT_SUMMARY               	pregnancy (early second trimester).
PR:INSTITUTE                     	RTI International
PR:DEPARTMENT                    	Discovery Sciences
PR:LABORATORY                    	Systems and Translational Sciences
PR:LAST_NAME                     	Burgess
PR:FIRST_NAME                    	Jason
PR:ADDRESS                       	3040 Cornwallis Rd, RTP, NC, 27609, USA
PR:EMAIL                         	jpb@rti.org
PR:PHONE                         	919-541-6700

ST:STUDY_TITLE                   	Who Developed Placental Abruption
ST:STUDY_TYPE                    	Metabolomics Biocrates Panel
ST:STUDY_SUMMARY                 	Placental abruption (PA) is an ischemic placental disorder that results from the
ST:STUDY_SUMMARY                 	premature separation of the placenta from the wall of the uterus before delivery
ST:STUDY_SUMMARY                 	of the fetus. This disorder is associated with pre-term delivery, fetal death,
ST:STUDY_SUMMARY                 	maternal hemorrhagic shock, and renal failure. Several physiologic disturbances,
ST:STUDY_SUMMARY                 	such as oxidative stress, carbohydrate/fatty acid metabolism, and mitochondrial
ST:STUDY_SUMMARY                 	dysfunction, have been associated with ischemic placental disorder as well as
ST:STUDY_SUMMARY                 	with placental abruption. This preliminary study proposes to identify
ST:STUDY_SUMMARY                 	metabolites associated with incident placental abruption using existing serum
ST:STUDY_SUMMARY                 	and clinical data from a previously studied cohort. Metabolomics analysis will
ST:STUDY_SUMMARY                 	be carried out on maternal serum (51 cases and 51 controls) collected in early
ST:STUDY_SUMMARY                 	pregnancy (early second trimester).

#SAMPLEPREP
SP:SAMPLEPREP_SUMMARY            	Sample Preparation Prior to Biocrates p180 Kit Plate Analysis: Serum samples
SP:SAMPLEPREP_SUMMARY            	were thawed on ice and pooled QC samples were prepared. Samples (study and
SP:SAMPLEPREP_SUMMARY            	pooled QC samples) were then diluted, vortexed, and transferred into properly
SP:SAMPLEPREP_SUMMARY            	labeled 2 mL Lo-Bind eppendorf tubes and dried on a lyophilizer overnight. The
SP:SAMPLEPREP_SUMMARY            	residue was reconstituted with 30 µL of PBS buffer. Samples were then vortexed
SP:SAMPLEPREP_SUMMARY            	and then centrifuged at room temperature and at 16,000 rcf for 4.0 minutes. All
SP:SAMPLEPREP_SUMMARY            	study samples and pooled QC samples were splitted into two AbsoluteIDQ p180
SP:SAMPLEPREP_SUMMARY            	Kit-96 wells plates (Plate 1502 and 1503). Biocrates Plate Preparation: The
SP:SAMPLEPREP_SUMMARY            	Biocrates p180 kit-96 wells plates were prepared following the AbsoluteIDQ p180
SP:SAMPLEPREP_SUMMARY            	Kit metabolomics procedure. Briefly, an internal standard mix was added to 95 of
SP:SAMPLEPREP_SUMMARY            	the 96 wells. Next, zero samples, QC standards and calibration standards were
SP:SAMPLEPREP_SUMMARY            	added to their corresponding wells. The study samples and pooled QC Samples were
SP:SAMPLEPREP_SUMMARY            	then added to the appropriate wells and dried for 30 minutes under nitrogen
SP:SAMPLEPREP_SUMMARY            	flow. The plate was derivatized using a 5% Phenylisothiocyanate (PITC) solution
SP:SAMPLEPREP_SUMMARY            	in (1:1:1) Ethanol:Pyridine:Water and, then, incubated for 20 minutes followed
SP:SAMPLEPREP_SUMMARY            	by a drying step under nitrogen flow. An extraction solvent (5 mM ammonium
SP:SAMPLEPREP_SUMMARY            	acetate in methanol) was added to all wells. The plate was then vortexed and
SP:SAMPLEPREP_SUMMARY            	filtrated by centrifugation. After centrifugation, 150 µL was removed and
SP:SAMPLEPREP_SUMMARY            	transferred to a second 96-well plate (LC-MS/MS plate). This second plate was
SP:SAMPLEPREP_SUMMARY            	diluted with 150 µL of HPLC grade water for a subsequent LC-MS/MS assay
SP:SAMPLEPREP_SUMMARY            	(analysis of amino acids and biogenic amines). All the wells in the original
SP:SAMPLEPREP_SUMMARY            	plate was diluted with 400 µL of flow injection analysis (FIA) Running Solvent
SP:SAMPLEPREP_SUMMARY            	for a FIA-MS analysis (lipids, acylcarnitines, and hexose analysis).
#CHROMATOGRAPHY
CH:CHROMATOGRAPHY_SUMMARY     	Biocrates P180 analysis combines a RP for positive mode MS , a flow injection
CH:CHROMATOGRAPHY_SUMMARY     	for both pos and neg mode MS
CH:CHROMATOGRAPHY_TYPE        	Biocrates P-180
CH:INSTRUMENT_NAME            	Agilent 1100
CH:COLUMN_NAME                	Agilent Eclipse XDB-C18 (3.0 x 100mm)
CH:FLOW_RATE                  	0.5 ml/min for RP and 0.2 ml/min for FIA
CH:COLUMN_TEMPERATURE         	50 c fro RP and RT for FIA
CH:SOLVENT_A                  	water with 0.2% formic acid
CH:SOLVENT_B                  	acetonitrile with 0.2% formic acid for RP, Methanol with Biocrates FIA Solvent
CH:COLUMN_PRESSURE            	30-120 bar for RP and 4-50 bar for FIA
CH:SAMPLE_INJECTION           	10 ul
